You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. The function should process a list of strings, each representing an email address, and return the number of unique domain names present. 

The input list is guaranteed to contain only valid email addresses in lowercase, with no additional formatting or special characters. The task requires you to:
1. Extract the domain part of each email address.
2. Identify the unique domains by using a set to store them.
3. Return the count of these unique domains.

Your solution should be efficient and scalable, even for large lists of email addresses. Ensure that the function is well-documented and includes comments explaining the logic.

### Highlighted Sections:

* **Step 1**: The function splits each email address into the domain part using the `split('@')` method. This is crucial for isolating the domain name from the rest of the email.
* **Step 2**: A set is used to store the domain names, ensuring that only unique domains are counted. This is essential for handling the uniqueness constraint.
* **Step 3**: The function returns the size of the set, which directly gives the number of unique domains.
* **Step 4**: The function is designed to handle large inputs efficiently, as sets in Python are optimized for such operations.
* **Step 5**: The function includes a detailed comment block explaining the logic and the purpose of each part of the code.

### Example Usage:
```python
emails = ['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']
print(count_unique_email_domains(emails))  # Output: 3
```

### Explanation:
- `email.split('@')[1]` extracts the domain part of the email.
- `set()` ensures that only unique domains are counted.
- `len(domains)` gives the number of unique domains.

This approach is efficient and scalable, even for large lists of email addresses.

Iteration 20: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions

You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. The function should:

1. **Process Input**: Accept a list of email addresses (strings), where each email is in lowercase and properly formatted (e.g., `user1@gmail.com`).
2. **Extract Domain**: For each email address, extract the domain part (e.g., `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`).
3. **Count Unique Domains**: Use a set to store the extracted domains to automatically handle duplicates.
4. **Return Result**: Return the number of unique domains found in the list.
5. **Constraints**:
   - Assume all email addresses are valid and in lowercase.
   - Do not use any external libraries or modules.
   - Ensure the function is efficient and handles edge cases (e.g., empty lists, invalid emails).

### Example Usage:

```python
emails = ['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']
print(count_unique_email_domains(emails))  # Output: 3
```

### Highlighted Sections:

* **Extracting the domain part** from each email address using `email.split('@')[1]` is crucial for isolating the domain name. This ensures that we only consider the domain part and not the local part (e.g., `user1` in `user1@gmail.com`).

* **Using a set** to store the domains ensures that we automatically handle duplicates, as sets only store unique elements. This is essential for counting the number of unique domains accurately.

### Additional Notes:

- The function should be **generalizable** to other similar tasks, such as extracting domain names from URLs or parsing other structured data.
- The function should be **efficient** and handle large input lists without performance degradation.
- The function should **handle edge cases** gracefully, such as empty input lists or invalid email formats.
- The function should be **clean and readable**, with clear comments and documentation where necessary.

Iteration 42: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions
You are tasked with solving a computational challenge involving subarray maximums. The problem requires you to compute the number of contiguous, non-empty subarrays in an array `A` of positive integers where the maximum value in the subarray is between two given integers `L` and `R` (inclusive). The constraints are:

- `A` is an array of positive integers with length up to 50,000.
- `L` and `R` are positive integers with `L <= R`.
- The goal is to count all valid subarrays where the maximum value is at least `L` and at most `R`.

### Task Description
You must provide an efficient solution to this problem, considering the constraints on the size of the input array. The solution must be optimal and handle large input sizes within acceptable time complexity.

### Key Constraints
- The solution must be efficient enough to handle an array of size up to 50,000.
- The solution must be able to handle repeated elements and ensure correctness for all valid inputs.
- The solution must be able to handle edge cases, such as when `L` and `R` are 0 or when the array contains elements outside the range `[L, R]`.

### Output Requirements
- The output must be a single integer representing the count of valid subarrays.
- The output must be formatted as a single integer in the response.

### Additional Requirements
- The solution must be implemented in Python.
- The solution must include a detailed explanation of the approach and the reasoning behind it.
- The solution must be well-documented and include comments where necessary.
- The solution must be tested with the provided example input to ensure correctness.

### Example Input
Input:
A = [2, 1, 4, 3]
L = 2
R = 3

Output:
3

### Explanation
The valid subarrays are:
- [2]
- [2, 1]
- [3]

### Solution Strategy
To efficiently solve this problem, we can use a sliding window approach. The idea is to maintain a window of elements where the maximum value is within the range `[L, R]`. As we expand the window, we ensure that the maximum value remains within the bounds, and we count the number of valid subarrays.

### Efficient Implementation
- We can use a deque to keep track of the maximum values in the current window efficiently.
- We iterate through the array and maintain a window where the maximum value is within the range `[L, R]`.
- For each element, we adjust the window to ensure the maximum value remains within the bounds.
- We count the number of valid subarrays as we expand the window.

### Edge Cases
- When `L` is 0 or `R` is 0.
- When the array contains elements that are outside the range `[L, R]`.
- When the array is empty.

### Final Output
The final output is a single integer representing the count of valid subarrays.

### Postscript
P.S. The solution must be implemented in Python and must be efficient enough to handle the maximum input size of 50,000 elements. The solution must also be tested with the provided example input to ensure correctness.
```python
def count_valid_subarrays(A, L, R):
    """
    Counts the number of contiguous, non-empty subarrays where the maximum value is between L and R (inclusive).
    
    Parameters:
    A (list of int): The input array of positive integers.
    L (int): The lower bound of the maximum value.
    R (int): The upper bound of the maximum value.
    
    Returns:
    int: The count of valid subarrays.
    """
    if not A:
        return 0
    
    n = len(A)
    count = 0
    max_deque = []
    left = 0
    
    for right in range(n):
        # Maintain the deque to store indices of elements in the current window
        while max_deque and A[max_deque[-1]] <= A[right]:
            max_deque.pop()
        max_deque.append(right)
        
        # Remove elements out of the window's range
        while max_deque[0] < left:
            max_deque.pop(0)
        
        # If the maximum value in the current window is within [L, R], increment the count
        if L <= A[max_deque[0]] <= R:
            count += n - right
        else:
            # If the maximum value is outside the range, adjust the window
            # This part may need adjustment based on the actual logic
            pass
    
    return count

Iteration 61: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Task Instructions

You are to analyze and refine a function intended to find the two closest numbers in a list of integers and return them along with the frequency of the smallest difference. The function is flawed and needs to be corrected. Your task is to:

1. **Identify the core functionality** of the original function and the **issues** it has.  
2. **Explain the problem** in detail, including:
   - Why the function fails to handle empty lists.
   - Why it does not sort the list.
   - Why it incorrectly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
3. **Propose a corrected approach** that:
   - Handles empty lists.
   - Sorts the list.
   - Correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
   - Identifies the two closest numbers and counts the frequency of the smallest difference.
4. **Provide a corrected code snippet** that implements the desired functionality.
5. **Discuss the flaws** in the original code and how they were addressed.
6. **Outline the correct solution** step-by-step, including:
   - How to sort the list.
   - How to iterate through adjacent elements.
   - How to find the smallest difference.
   - How to store and return the two closest numbers and their frequency.
7. **Include a detailed explanation** of the corrected code, its logic, and its benefits.
8. **Conclude with a summary** of the key points and the improvements made.

**Example Output Format**:
<<Corrected Function for Finding Closest Numbers and Their Frequency>>

The function should:
- Handle empty lists by returning an empty list or appropriate error.
- Sort the input list in ascending order.
- Iterate through adjacent elements to compute differences.
- Identify the two closest numbers and count the frequency of the smallest difference.
- Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

The original function had the following flaws:
- It did not handle empty lists.
- It did not sort the input list.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements.

The corrected function will:
- Sort the list.
- Compare adjacent elements to find the smallest difference.
- Track the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference.

**Corrected Code Snippet**:
```python
def find_two_closest_numbers_and_frequency(numbers):
    if not numbers:
        return []
    
    numbers.sort()
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        current_diff = abs(numbers[i+1] - numbers[i])
        if current_diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = current_diff
            closest_numbers = [numbers[i], numbers[i+1]]
        elif current_diff == min_diff:
            closest_numbers.append((numbers[i], numbers[i+1]))
    
    return closest_numbers, min_diff
```

**Explanation of the Corrected Solution**:
1. The function first checks if the input list is empty and returns an empty list if so.
2. The list is sorted to enable comparison of adjacent elements.
3. The smallest difference is initialized to infinity.
4. The function iterates through the sorted list, comparing each pair of adjacent elements.
5. The smallest difference is tracked, and the two closest numbers are stored.
6. If multiple pairs have the same smallest difference, all are counted.
7. The function returns the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

**Flaws in the Original Code**:
- The original function did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

**Conclusion**:
The corrected function ensures that the list is sorted, handles empty inputs, and correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements. It provides the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference, making it a robust solution for the task.

Iteration 66: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Task Instructions

You are to analyze and refine a function intended to find the two closest numbers in a list of integers and return them along with the frequency of the smallest difference. The function is flawed and needs to be corrected. Your task is to:

1. **Identify the core functionality** of the original function and the **issues** it has.  
2. **Explain the problem** in detail, including:
   - Why the function fails to handle empty lists.
   - Why it does not sort the list.
   - Why it incorrectly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
3. **Propose a corrected approach** that:
   - Handles empty lists.
   - Sorts the list.
   - Correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
   - Identifies the two closest numbers and counts the frequency of the smallest difference.
4. **Provide a corrected code snippet** that implements the desired functionality.
5. **Discuss the flaws** in the original code and how they were addressed.
6. **Outline the correct solution** step-by-step, including:
   - How to sort the list.
   - How to iterate through adjacent elements.
   - How to find the smallest difference.
   - How to store and return the two closest numbers and their frequency.
7. **Include a detailed explanation** of the corrected code, its logic, and its benefits.
8. **Conclude with a summary** of the key points and the improvements made.

**Example Output Format**:
<<Corrected Function for Finding Closest Numbers and Their Frequency>>

The function should:
- Handle empty lists by returning an empty list or appropriate error.
- Sort the input list in ascending order.
- Iterate through adjacent elements to compute differences.
- Identify the two closest numbers and count the frequency of the smallest difference.
- Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

The original function had the following flaws:
- It did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

The corrected function will:
- Sort the list.
- Compare adjacent elements to find the smallest difference.
- Track the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference.

**Corrected Code Snippet**:
```python
def find_two_closest_numbers_and_frequency(numbers):
    if not numbers:
        return []
    
    numbers.sort()
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        current_diff = abs(numbers[i+1] - numbers[i])
        if current_diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = current_diff
            closest_numbers = [numbers[i], numbers[i+1]]
        elif current_diff == min_diff:
            closest_numbers.append((numbers[i], numbers[i+1]))
    
    return closest_numbers, min_diff
```

**Explanation of the Corrected Solution**:
1. The function first checks if the input list is empty and returns an empty list if so.
2. The list is sorted to enable comparison of adjacent elements.
3. The smallest difference is initialized to infinity.
4. The function iterates through the sorted list, comparing each pair of adjacent elements.
5. The smallest difference is tracked, and the two closest numbers are stored.
6. If multiple pairs have the same smallest difference, all are counted.
7. The function returns the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

**Flaws in the Original Code**:
- The original function did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

**Conclusion**:
The corrected function ensures that the list is sorted, handles empty inputs, and correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements. It provides the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference, making it a robust solution for the task.

Iteration 70: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Task Instructions

You are to analyze and refine a function intended to find the two closest numbers in a list of integers and return them along with the frequency of the smallest difference. The function is flawed and needs to be corrected. Your task is to:

1. **Identify the core functionality** of the original function and the **issues** it has.  
2. **Explain the problem** in detail, including:
   - Why the function fails to handle empty lists.
   - Why it does not sort the list.
   - Why it incorrectly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
3. **Propose a corrected approach** that:
   - Handles empty lists.
   - Sorts the list.
   - Correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
   - Identifies the two closest numbers and counts the frequency of the smallest difference.
4. **Provide a corrected code snippet** that implements the desired functionality.
5. **Discuss the flaws** in the original code and how they were addressed.
6. **Outline the correct solution** step-by-step, including:
   - How to sort the list.
   - How to iterate through adjacent elements.
   - How to find the smallest difference.
   - How to store and return the two closest numbers and their frequency.
7. **Include a detailed explanation** of the corrected code, its logic, and its benefits.
8. **Conclude with a summary** of the key points and the improvements made.

**Example Output Format**:
<<Corrected Function for Finding Closest Numbers and Their Frequency>>

The function should:
- Handle empty lists by returning an empty list or appropriate error.
- Sort the input list in ascending order.
- Iterate through adjacent elements to compute differences.
- Identify the two closest numbers and count the frequency of the smallest difference.
- Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

The original function had the following flaws:
- It did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

The corrected function will:
- Sort the list.
- Compare adjacent elements to find the smallest difference.
- Track the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference.

**Corrected Code Snippet**:
```python
def find_two_closest_numbers_and_frequency(numbers):
    if not numbers:
        return []
    
    numbers.sort()
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        current_diff = abs(numbers[i+1] - numbers[i])
        if current_diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = current_diff
            closest_numbers = [numbers[i], numbers[i+1]]
        elif current_diff == min_diff:
            closest_numbers.append((numbers[i], numbers[i+1]))
    
    return closest_numbers, min_diff

1. **Identify the core functionality** of the original function and the **issues** it has.

   - Why the function fails to handle empty lists.
   - Why it does not sort the list.

   - Handles empty lists.

   - How to sort the list.

   - How to find the smallest difference.

**Example Output Format**:
<<Corrected Function for Finding Closest Numbers and Their Frequency>>

The function should:
- Handle empty lists by returning an empty list or appropriate error.
- Sort the input list in ascending order.
- Iterate through adjacent elements to compute differences.
- Identify the two closest numbers and count the frequency of the smallest difference.
- Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

The original function had the following flaws:
- It did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

- Sort the list.
- Compare adjacent elements to find the smallest difference.
- Track the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference.

**Corrected Code Snippet**:
```python
def find_two_closest_numbers_and_frequency(numbers):
    if not numbers:
        return []
    
    numbers.sort()
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        current_diff = abs(numbers[i+1] - numbers[i])
        if current_diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = current_diff
            closest_numbers = [numbers[i], numbers[i+1]]
        elif current_diff == min_diff:
            closest_numbers.append((numbers[i], numbers[i+1]))
    
    return closest_numbers, min_diff
```

**Explanation of the Corrected Solution**:
1. The function first checks if the input list is empty and returns an empty list if so.
2. The list is sorted to enable comparison of adjacent elements.
3. The smallest difference is initialized to infinity.
4. The function iterates through the sorted list, comparing each pair of adjacent elements.
5. The smallest difference is tracked, and the two closest numbers are stored.
6. If multiple pairs have the same smallest difference, all are counted.
7. The function returns the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

**Flaws in the Original Code**:
- The original function did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

**Conclusion**:
The corrected function ensures that the list is sorted, handles empty inputs, and correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements. It provides the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference, making it a robust solution for the task.

   - The new column must be **on the right**.

Iteration 87: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Task Instructions

You are to analyze and refine a function intended to find the two closest numbers in a list of integers and return them along with the frequency of the smallest difference. The function is flawed and needs to be corrected. Your task is to:

1. **Identify the core functionality** of the original function and the **issues** it has.  
2. **Explain the problem** in detail, including:
   - Why the function fails to handle empty lists.
   - Why it does not sort the list.
   - Why it incorrectly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
3. **Propose a corrected approach** that:
   - Handles empty lists.
   - Sorts the list.
   - Correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
   - Identifies the two closest numbers and counts the frequency of the smallest difference.
4. **Provide a corrected code snippet** that implements the desired functionality.
5. **Discuss the flaws** in the original code and how they were addressed.
6. **Outline the correct solution** step-by-step, including:
   - How to sort the list.
   - How to iterate through adjacent elements.
   - How to find the smallest difference.
   - How to store and return the two closest numbers and their frequency.
7. **Include a detailed explanation** of the corrected code, its logic, and its benefits.
8. **Conclude with a summary** of the key points and the improvements made.

**Example Output Format**:
<<Corrected Function for Finding Closest Numbers and Their Frequency>>

The function should:
- Handle empty lists by returning an empty list or appropriate error.
- Sort the input list in ascending order.
- Iterate through adjacent elements to compute differences.
- Identify the two closest numbers and count the frequency of the smallest difference.
- Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

The original function had the following flaws:
- It did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

The corrected function will:
- Sort the list.
- Compare adjacent elements to find the smallest difference.
- Track the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference.

**Corrected Code Snippet**:
```python
def find_two_closest_numbers_and_frequency(numbers):
    if not numbers:
        return []
    
    numbers.sort()
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        current_diff = abs(numbers[i+1] - numbers[i])
        if current_diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = current_diff
            closest_numbers = [numbers[i], numbers[i+1]]
        elif current_diff == min_diff:
            closest_numbers.append((numbers[i], numbers[i+1]))
    
    return closest_numbers, min_diff
```

**Explanation of the Corrected Solution**:
1. The function first checks if the input list is empty and returns an empty list if so.
2. The list is sorted to enable comparison of adjacent elements.
3. The smallest difference is initialized to infinity.
4. The function iterates through the sorted list, comparing each pair of adjacent elements.
5. The smallest difference is tracked, and the two closest numbers are stored.
6. If multiple pairs have the same smallest difference, all are counted.
7. The function returns the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

**Flaws in the Original Code**:
- The original function did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

**Conclusion**:
The corrected function ensures that the list is sorted, handles empty inputs, and correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements. It provides the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference, making it a robust solution for the task.

def find_closest_numbers(nums):  
    if not nums or len(nums) < 2:  
        return None, None  
    nums.sort()  
    min_diff = float('inf')  
    closest_pair = None  
    for i in range(len(nums) - 1):  
        current = nums[i]  
        next_val = nums[i + 1]  
        diff = next_val - current  
        if diff < min_diff:  
            min_diff = diff  
            closest_pair = (current, next_val)  
    return closest_pair, min_diff

def find_closest_numbers(nums):  
    if not nums or len(nums) < 2:  
        return None, None  
    nums.sort()  
    min_diff = float('inf')  
    closest_pair = None

        next_val = nums[i + 1]  
        diff = next_val - current  
        if diff < min_diff:  
            min_diff = diff  
            closest_pair = (current, next_val)  
    return closest_pair, min_diff

You are to analyze and refine a function that is intended to find the two closest numbers in a list of integers and return them along with the frequency of the smallest difference. The function is flawed and needs to be refined to handle edge cases such as empty lists, lists with only one element, and duplicate values. The function also fails to properly calculate the smallest difference and does not count the frequency of that difference.  

### Task Description  
The function must:  
1. **Handle edge cases**:  
   - Return an error or a specific value if the input list is empty or contains only one element.  
   - Handle duplicate values correctly, ensuring that the same number is not counted more than once in the pair.  

2. **Sort the list**:  
   - Sort the list of integers in ascending order to efficiently find the closest pairs.  

3. **Find the closest pair**:  
   - Iterate through the sorted list to compare adjacent elements and find the pair with the smallest difference.  

4. **Calculate the smallest difference**:  
   - Compute the difference between each pair of adjacent elements in the sorted list.  

5. **Count the frequency of the smallest difference**:  
   - Count how many times the smallest difference occurs in the list.  

6. **Return the result**:  
   - Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.  

### Refinement Requirements  
- The function must not return any values for empty or single-element lists.  
- The function must correctly handle duplicates and ensure that the same number is not considered more than once in the pair.  
- The function must correctly calculate the smallest difference and count its frequency.  

### Additional Constraints  
- The function must be implemented in a way that is efficient for large lists.  
- The function must be robust to invalid inputs (e.g., non-integer values).  

### Example Usage  
For input `[5, 1, 3, 7, 9]`, the function should return `(3, 5, 2)` as the two closest numbers and `2` as the frequency of the smallest difference.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information  
- The task involves sorting and comparing adjacent elements in a list, which is a common technique in algorithms for finding closest pairs.  
- The frequency of the smallest difference requires a counting mechanism, which is a common requirement in data analysis and statistics.

Iteration 102: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Task Instructions

You are to analyze and refine a function intended to find the two closest numbers in a list of integers and return them along with the frequency of the smallest difference. The function is flawed and needs to be corrected. Your task is to:

1. **Identify the core functionality** of the original function and the **issues** it has.  
2. **Explain the problem** in detail, including:
   - Why the function fails to handle empty lists.
   - Why it does not sort the list.
   - Why it incorrectly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
3. **Propose a corrected approach** that:
   - Handles empty lists.
   - Sorts the list.
   - Correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
   - Identifies the two closest numbers and counts the frequency of the smallest difference.
4. **Provide a corrected code snippet** that implements the desired functionality.
5. **Discuss the flaws** in the original code and how they were addressed.
6. **Outline the correct solution** step-by-step, including:
   - How to sort the list.
   - How to iterate through adjacent elements.
   - How to find the smallest difference.
   - How to store and return the two closest numbers and their frequency.
7. **Include a detailed explanation** of the corrected code, its logic, and its benefits.
8. **Conclude with a summary** of the key points and the improvements made.

**Example Output Format**:
<<Corrected Function for Finding Closest Numbers and Their Frequency>>

The function should:
- Handle empty lists by returning an empty list or appropriate error.
- Sort the input list in ascending order.
- Iterate through adjacent elements to compute differences.
- Identify the two closest numbers and count the frequency of the smallest difference.
- Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

The original function had the following flaws:
- It did not handle empty lists.
- It did not sort the input list.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements.

The corrected function will:
- Sort the list.
- Compare adjacent elements to find the smallest difference.
- Track the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference.

**Corrected Code Snippet**:
```python
def find_two_closest_numbers_and_frequency(numbers):
    if not numbers:
        return []
    
    numbers.sort()
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        current_diff = abs(numbers[i+1] - numbers[i])
        if current_diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = current_diff
            closest_numbers = [numbers[i], numbers[i+1]]
        elif current_diff == min_diff:
            closest_numbers.append((numbers[i], numbers[i+1]))
    
    return closest_numbers, min_diff
```

**Explanation of the Corrected Solution**:
1. The function first checks if the input list is empty and returns an empty list if so.
2. The list is sorted to enable comparison of adjacent elements.
3. The smallest difference is initialized to infinity.
4. The function iterates through the sorted list, comparing each pair of adjacent elements.
5. The smallest difference is tracked, and the two closest numbers are stored.
6. If multiple pairs have the same smallest difference, all are counted.
7. The function returns the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

**Flaws in the Original Code**:
- The original function did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

**Conclusion**:
The corrected function ensures that the list is sorted, handles empty inputs, and correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements. It provides the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference, making it a robust solution for the task.

Sec. 2  
The function should first sort the list to make it easier to compare consecutive elements. It should then iterate through the sorted list, calculate the differences between consecutive elements, and track the minimum difference. Once the minimum difference is found, the function should identify the pair of numbers with that difference and count how many times this minimum difference occurs.  

Sec. 3  
The core functionality of the function involves sorting the list, iterating through it, and comparing consecutive elements. The main issues with the original code include not handling duplicate elements correctly, not accounting for edge cases like empty lists or lists with only one element, and not efficiently finding the minimum difference.  

Sec. 4  
The original code may have flaws in how it handles duplicates and edge cases. For example, if the list has only one element, the function should return that element as the only possible pair. If the list is empty, the function should return an appropriate error message or handle it gracefully.  

Sec. 5  
The function should also handle cases where multiple pairs have the same minimum difference. For example, if the list contains [1, 3, 5, 7], the minimum difference is 2, and the pairs (1,3), (3,5), (5,7) all have this difference. The frequency should count how many such pairs exist.  

Sec. 6  
The function should return the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference. If there are multiple pairs with the same minimum difference, the function should return all of them. If no pairs are found (e.g., the list has only one element), the function should return an appropriate message.  

Sec. 7  
The original code may not have handled cases where the list is empty or contains only one element. The corrected code should include checks for these scenarios and return appropriate results. For example, if the list is empty, the function should return an error message or a message indicating that no pairs can be found.  

Sec. 8  
The function should be efficient, especially for large lists. Sorting the list takes O(n log n) time, and iterating through it takes O(n) time, making the overall time complexity O(n log n). This is efficient for most practical applications.  

Sec. 9  
The function should return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference. If the list contains duplicate numbers, the function should count how many times the smallest difference occurs. For example, if the list is [2, 2, 4, 4], the minimum difference is 2, and the frequency is 2.  

Sec. 10  
The corrected function should be implemented in Python, with clear comments explaining each step. The function should handle all edge cases and return the correct output for any valid input. The function should also be tested with various examples to ensure correctness.

Iteration 109: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Task Instructions

You are to analyze and refine a function intended to translate a given English sentence into Spanish, adhering to specific formatting and constraints. The function is flawed and needs to be corrected. Your task is to:

1. **Identify the core functionality** of the original function and the **issues** it has.  
2. **Explain the problem** in detail, including:
   - Why the function fails to handle empty sentences.
   - Why it does not follow the required capitalization rules.
   - Why it does not wrap words in double angular brackets.
   - Why it does not adhere to the "less than 3 letters" constraint.
3. **Propose a corrected approach** that:
   - Handles empty sentences.
   - Follows the required capitalization rules.
   - Wraps every word in double angular brackets.
   - Adheres to the "less than 3 letters" constraint.
   - Translates the English sentence into Spanish correctly.
4. **Provide a corrected code snippet** that implements the desired functionality.
5. **Discuss the flaws** in the original code and how they were addressed.
6. **Outline the correct solution** step-by-step, including:
   - How to handle empty inputs.
   - How to wrap words in double angular brackets.
   - How to ensure proper capitalization.
   - How to adhere to the "less than 3 letters" constraint.
   - How to translate the sentence into Spanish.
7. **Include a detailed explanation** of the corrected code, its logic, and its benefits.
8. **Conclude with a summary** of the key points and the improvements made.

**Example Output Format**:
<<Translated Sentence>>

The function should:
- Handle empty sentences by returning an empty string or appropriate error.
- Wrap every word in double angular brackets.
- Follow the required capitalization rules.
- Adhere to the "less than 3 letters" constraint.
- Translate the English sentence into Spanish correctly.

The original function had the following flaws:
- It did not handle empty sentences, which could lead to errors or incorrect translations.
- It did not wrap words in double angular brackets, violating the formatting requirements.
- It did not follow the required capitalization rules.
- It did not adhere to the "less than 3 letters" constraint, leading to invalid outputs.

The corrected function will:
- Handle empty inputs.
- Wrap words in double angular brackets.
- Follow proper capitalization.
- Adhere to the "less than 3 letters" constraint.
- Translate the English sentence into Spanish correctly.

**Corrected Code Snippet**:
```python
def translate_to_spanish(sentence):
    if not sentence:
        return ""
    
    # Wrap each word in double angular brackets
    translated = []
    for word in sentence.split():
        translated.append(f"<<{word}>>")
    
    # Capitalize the first letter of each word
    translated = [word.capitalize() for word in translated]
    
    # Join the translated words into a single string
    return " ".join(translated)
```

**Explanation of the Corrected Solution**:
1. The function first checks if the input sentence is empty and returns an empty string if so.
2. It splits the sentence into words and wraps each word in double angular brackets.
3. It capitalizes the first letter of each word to meet the required formatting.
4. It joins the translated words into a single string and returns it.

**Flaws in the Original Code**:
- The original function did not handle empty sentences, leading to potential errors.
- It did not wrap words in double angular brackets, violating the formatting requirements.
- It did not follow the required capitalization rules.
- It did not adhere to the "less than 3 letters" constraint, leading to invalid outputs.

**Conclusion**:
The corrected function ensures that the input is handled correctly, formatting is adhered to, and the translation is accurate. It provides a robust solution for translating English sentences into Spanish while meeting all specified constraints.

Iteration 112: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Task Instructions

You are to analyze and refine a function intended to find the two closest numbers in a list of integers and return them along with the frequency of the smallest difference. The function is flawed and needs to be corrected. Your task is to:

1. **Identify the core functionality** of the original function and the **issues** it has.  
2. **Explain the problem** in detail, including:
   - Why the function fails to handle empty lists.
   - Why it does not sort the list.
   - Why it incorrectly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
3. **Propose a corrected approach** that:
   - Handles empty lists.
   - Sorts the list.
   - Correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
   - Identifies the two closest numbers and counts the frequency of the smallest difference.
4. **Provide a corrected code snippet** that implements the desired functionality.
5. **Discuss the flaws** in the original code and how they were addressed.
6. **Outline the correct solution** step-by-step, including:
   - How to sort the list.
   - How to iterate through adjacent elements.
   - How to find the smallest difference.
   - How to store and return the two closest numbers and their frequency.
7. **Include a detailed explanation** of the corrected code, its logic, and its benefits.
8. **Conclude with a summary** of the key points and the improvements made.

**Example Output Format**:
<<Corrected Function for Finding Closest Numbers and Their Frequency>>

The function should:
- Handle empty lists by returning an empty list or appropriate error.
- Sort the input list in ascending order.
- Iterate through adjacent elements to compute differences.
- Identify the two closest numbers and count the frequency of the smallest difference.
- Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

The original function had the following flaws:
- It did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

The corrected function will:
- Sort the list.
- Compare adjacent elements to find the smallest difference.
- Track the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference.

**Corrected Code Snippet**:
```python
def find_two_closest_numbers_and_frequency(numbers):
    if not numbers:
        return []
    
    numbers.sort()
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        current_diff = abs(numbers[i+1] - numbers[i])
        if current_diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = current_diff
            closest_numbers = [numbers[i], numbers[i+1]]
        elif current_diff == min_diff:
            closest_numbers.append((numbers[i], numbers[i+1]))
    
    return closest_numbers, min_diff
```

**Explanation of the Corrected Solution**:
1. The function first checks if the input list is empty and returns an empty list if so.
2. The list is sorted to enable comparison of adjacent elements.
3. The smallest difference is initialized to infinity.
4. The function iterates through the sorted list, comparing each pair of adjacent elements.
5. The smallest difference is tracked, and the two closest numbers are stored.
6. If multiple pairs have the same smallest difference, all are counted.
7. The function returns the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

**Flaws in the Original Code**:
- The original function did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

**Conclusion**:
The corrected function ensures that the list is sorted, handles empty inputs, and correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements. It provides the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference, making it a robust solution for the task.

Iteration 114: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Instruction

You are tasked with writing a function that finds the two closest numbers in a list of integers and returns them along with the frequency of the smallest difference. The function must handle empty lists and must sort the list before comparing adjacent elements to find the smallest difference. 

### Core Functionality:
- **Handle empty lists**: The function must return an appropriate message or value if the input list is empty.
- **Sort the list**: The list must be sorted before comparing adjacent elements to efficiently find the closest numbers.
- **Calculate differences between adjacent elements**: The function must iterate through the sorted list and compute the differences between each pair of adjacent elements.
- **Find the smallest difference**: The function must track the smallest difference and the corresponding numbers.
- **Count the frequency of the smallest difference**: The function must count how many times the smallest difference occurs in the list.
- **Return results**: The function must return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

### Flaws in the Original Code:
1. **Not handling empty lists**: The original code does not check if the input list is empty, which can lead to errors or incorrect results.
2. **Not sorting the list**: The original code does not sort the input list, which is necessary to find the closest numbers efficiently.
3. **Not correctly calculating differences between adjacent elements**: The original code does not properly compute the differences between adjacent elements in the list.

### Corrected Approach:
1. **Sort the input list**: The list must be sorted to enable efficient comparison of adjacent elements.
2. **Handle empty lists**: Add a check to ensure the list is not empty before proceeding.
3. **Calculate differences between adjacent elements**: Iterate through the sorted list and compute the differences between each pair of adjacent elements.
4. **Find the smallest difference**: Track the smallest difference and the corresponding numbers.
5. **Count the frequency of the smallest difference**: Count how many times the smallest difference occurs in the list.
6. **Return the results**: Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

### Corrected Code Snippet:
```python
def find_two_closest_numbers_and_frequency(numbers):
    if not numbers:
        return "Empty list"
    
    numbers.sort()
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        diff = numbers[i+1] - numbers[i]
        if diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = diff
            closest_numbers = [numbers[i], numbers[i+1]]
        elif diff == min_diff:
            closest_numbers.append((numbers[i], numbers[i+1]))
    
    return closest_numbers, min_diff, len(closest_numbers)
```

### Expected Output:
- The two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

### Explanation:
- **Sorting**: The list is sorted to enable efficient comparison of adjacent elements.
- **Handling empty lists**: The function returns a message if the list is empty.
- **Finding closest numbers**: The function iterates through the sorted list and computes the differences between adjacent elements to find the smallest difference.
- **Counting frequency**: The function counts how many times the smallest difference occurs in the list.

### Key Points and Improvements:
- The function now properly handles empty lists and sorts the input list before comparing adjacent elements.
- The function correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements and tracks the smallest difference and its frequency.
- The corrected code returns the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference as required.

Iteration 115: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Instructions

You are to act as an assistant that follows specific formatting and content guidelines to generate a response that meets all the constraints provided. The task involves analyzing a dataset of countries with associated political instability scores and interest rates over a set period. The goal is to write a Python function that filters the data based on a given threshold and returns a list of dictionaries containing the relevant information for countries that meet the condition.

### Input Format
- `data`: A list of dictionaries where each dictionary represents a country with keys `'country'`, `'year'`, `'instability_score'`, and `'interest_rate'`.
- `threshold`: A float representing the political instability score threshold.

### Output Format
- A list of dictionaries, each containing the `'country'`, `'year'`, `'instability_score'`, and `'interest_rate'` for years where the instability score was above the given threshold.

### Task Description
You are to implement a Python function that:
1. Filters the input data to include only those entries where the `instability_score` is greater than the given threshold.
2. Returns a list of dictionaries containing the filtered data.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information
- The function must handle floating-point numbers for both instability scores and interest rates.
- The function must ensure that the output is a list of dictionaries with the exact keys `'country'`, `'year'`, `'instability_score'`, and `'interest_rate'`.
- The function must be written in Python and must be enclosed in a code block.
- The function must be tested with the provided example data and expected output.

### Generalizable Strategy
- The function uses list comprehension to filter the data based on the threshold.
- The function returns the filtered data in the required format.

### Example
```python
def analyze_countries(data, threshold):
    filtered_data = [
        {
            'country': row['country'],
            'year': row['year'],
            'instability_score': row['instability_score'],
            'interest_rate': row['interest_rate']
        }
        for row in data
        if row['instability_score'] > threshold
    ]
    return filtered_data
```

### Feedback
- The first word of your response should be the word "ride".
- The response must contain at least two placeholders represented by square brackets.
- The response must contain a title, wrapped in double angular brackets, such as <<poem of joy>>.
- The response must include the span of words between indices 452 and 649 (character indices), if applicable.

Iteration 122: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## Task Instructions

You are to analyze and refine a function intended to find the two closest numbers in a list of integers and return them along with the frequency of the smallest difference. The function is flawed and needs to be corrected. Your task is to:

1. **Identify the core functionality** of the original function and the **issues** it has.  
2. **Explain the problem** in detail, including:
   - Why the function fails to handle empty lists.
   - Why it does not sort the list.
   - Why it incorrectly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
3. **Propose a corrected approach** that:
   - Handles empty lists.
   - Sorts the list.
   - Correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements.
   - Identifies the two closest numbers and counts the frequency of the smallest difference.
4. **Provide a corrected code snippet** that implements the desired functionality.
5. **Discuss the flaws** in the original code and how they were addressed.
6. **Outline the correct solution** step-by-step, including:
   - How to sort the list.
   - How to iterate through adjacent elements.
   - How to find the smallest difference.
   - How to store and return the two closest numbers and their frequency.
7. **Include a detailed explanation** of the corrected code, its logic, and its benefits.
8. **Conclude with a summary** of the key points and the improvements made.

**Example Output Format**:
<<Corrected Function for Finding Closest Numbers and Their Frequency>>

The function should:
- Handle empty lists by returning an empty list or appropriate error.
- Sort the input list in ascending order.
- Iterate through adjacent elements to compute differences.
- Identify the two closest numbers and count the frequency of the smallest difference.
- Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

The original function had the following flaws:
- It did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

The corrected function will:
- Sort the list.
- Compare adjacent elements to find the smallest difference.
- Track the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference.

**Corrected Code Snippet**:
```python
def find_two_closest_numbers_and_frequency(numbers):
    if not numbers:
        return []
    
    numbers.sort()
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        current_diff = abs(numbers[i+1] - numbers[i])
        if current_diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = current_diff
            closest_numbers = [numbers[i], numbers[i+1]]
        elif current_diff == min_diff:
            closest_numbers.append((numbers[i], numbers[i+1]))
    
    return closest_numbers, min_diff
```

**Explanation of the Corrected Solution**:
1. The function first checks if the input list is empty and returns an empty list if so.
2. The list is sorted to enable comparison of adjacent elements.
3. The smallest difference is initialized to infinity.
4. The function iterates through the sorted list, comparing each pair of adjacent elements.
5. The smallest difference is tracked, and the two closest numbers are stored.
6. If multiple pairs have the same smallest difference, all are counted.
7. The function returns the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

**Flaws in the Original Code**:
- The original function did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

**Conclusion**:
The corrected function ensures that the list is sorted, handles empty inputs, and correctly calculates the differences between adjacent elements. It provides the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference, making it a robust solution for the task.

Iteration 123: Proposed new text for system_prompt: **Task Instruction:**  
You are to analyze and refine a function that is intended to find the two closest numbers in a list of integers and return them along with the frequency of the smallest difference. The function is flawed and needs to be corrected to handle edge cases such as empty lists, lists with only one element, and duplicate values. The function must also correctly calculate the smallest difference and count the frequency of that difference.

**Core Requirements:**  
1. **Input Handling:**  
   - The function must handle empty lists, lists with only one element, and lists with multiple elements.  
   - If the list has fewer than two elements, the function should return an appropriate error message or handle it according to the problem's requirements.

2. **Sorting:**  
   - The function must sort the list of integers in ascending order to efficiently find the closest pairs.

3. **Finding Closest Pairs:**  
   - Iterate through the sorted list to find adjacent pairs of integers.  
   - For each pair, calculate the absolute difference between the two integers.  
   - Track the smallest difference found and the frequency of this difference in the list.

4. **Returning Results:**  
   - If a valid pair is found (i.e., there are at least two elements), return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.  
   - If the list has only one element, return an appropriate message (e.g., "The list contains only one element; no pairs can be found.").  
   - If the list is empty, return an appropriate message (e.g., "The list is empty; no pairs can be found.").  

5. **Edge Cases:**  
   - Handle cases where the list contains duplicate values.  
   - Ensure that the function does not count the same difference multiple times if it occurs in multiple pairs.  
   - If multiple pairs have the same smallest difference, all of them should be counted in the frequency.

6. **Output Format:**  
   - Return the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference in the format:  
     ```  
     (closest number 1, closest number 2, frequency of smallest difference)  
     ```  
   - If no valid pairs can be found, return an appropriate message.

**Additional Notes:**  
- The function must be implemented in a way that is efficient for large lists.  
- The function should not assume any specific data types for the input list.  
- The function should not modify the input list.  
- If the list contains non-integer values, the function should handle them appropriately (e.g., by filtering out non-integer values or raising an error).  

**Correct Approach:**  
1. Sort the list of integers.  
2. Iterate through the sorted list and compare adjacent elements.  
3. Track the smallest difference and the frequency of that difference.  
4. Return the results as specified.  

**Example Usage:**  
```python
def find_closest_numbers_and_frequency(sorted_list):
    if len(sorted_list) < 2:
        return "The list must contain at least two elements."
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    frequency = 0
    for i in range(len(sorted_list) - 1):
        current_diff = abs(sorted_list[i] - sorted_list[i + 1])
        if current_diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = current_diff
            closest_numbers = [sorted_list[i], sorted_list[i + 1]]
            frequency = 1
        elif current_diff == min_diff:
            frequency += 1
    return closest_numbers, frequency

- Sort the input list in ascending order.

- Identify the two closest numbers and count the frequency of the smallest difference.

The original function had the following flaws:
- It did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
- It incorrectly calculated the differences between adjacent elements, possibly by using non-adjacent pairs or not considering all elements.

The corrected function will:
- Sort the list.
- Compare adjacent elements to find the smallest difference.
- Track the two closest numbers and their frequency of the smallest difference.

**Corrected Code Snippet**:
```python
def find_two_closest_numbers_and_frequency(numbers):
    if not numbers:
        return []
    
    numbers.sort()
    min_diff = float('inf')
    closest_numbers = []
    
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        current_diff = abs(numbers[i+1] - numbers[i])
        if current_diff < min_diff:
            min_diff = current_diff
            closest_numbers = [numbers[i], numbers[i+1]]
        elif current_diff == min_diff:
            closest_numbers.append((numbers[i], numbers[i+1]))
    
    return closest_numbers, min_diff
```

**Explanation of the Corrected Solution**:
1. The function first checks if the input list is empty and returns an empty list if so.
2. The list is sorted to enable comparison of adjacent elements.
3. The smallest difference is initialized to infinity.
4. The function iterates through the sorted list, comparing each pair of adjacent elements.
5. The smallest difference is tracked, and the two closest numbers are stored.
6. If multiple pairs have the same smallest difference, all are counted.
7. The function returns the two closest numbers and the frequency of the smallest difference.

- The original function did not handle empty lists, which could lead to errors or incorrect results.
- It did not sort the list, so the comparison of adjacent elements was not done in the correct order.
